Scene/Seizure Documentation\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 1.1 | Record seizure paperwork (warrant, date/time, location, officers, chain of custody log). | Creates legal pedigree and protects admissibility. | Standard forensic log template (Excel/Word). |\n| 1.2 | Photograph the device in its original state and the forensic bag. | Visual proof of condition at seizure. | Digital camera or forensic imaging kit. |\n| 1.3 | Note device condition (screen, battery, charging port, SIM tray). | Helps anticipate acquisition challenges. | Observation notes. |\n\n---\n\n### 2. Initial Forensic\u2011Safe Acquisition\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 2.1 | **Create a forensic image of the internal storage** (eMMC/SSD). | Raw, bit\u2011by\u2011bit copy preserves all artefacts, including deleted data. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer (Android 14 support)<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic Detective \u2013 \u201cPhysical Acquisition\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fMagnet AXIOM \u2013 \u201cPhysical Copy\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fIf device is unlockable, use `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f backup.ab` + `adb backup -n`. |\n| 2.2 | Compute and record SHA\u2011256 & MD5 of the image. | Enables later integrity verification. | `sha256sum img.dd` / `md5sum img.dd` (Linux) or FTK Imager. |\n| 2.3 | If the device is **locked** and you cannot unlock it, perform a **hardware\u2011level acquisition** (e.g., using a write\u2011blocker compatible with Samsung eMMC). | Some forensic tools can extract a full image even when the OS is locked. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer \u2013 \u201cHardware Acquisition\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic \u2013 \u201cDevice Acquisition\u201d (if supported). |\n| 2.4 | Verify image integrity with the original hash values. | Confirms that the image was not corrupted in transit. | Same tools as 2.2. |\n| 2.5 | Store the image in a write\u2011protected, access\u2011controlled storage (e.g., forensic server). | Prevents accidental tampering. | Encrypted NAS or dedicated forensic workstation. |\n\n---\n\n### 3. Device De\u2011Encryption (If Needed)\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 3.1 | Determine encryption status (Android 14 uses **File Based Encryption (FBE)** + **Device Owner** keys). | If the image is encrypted, you cannot read useful files. | `dd` + `ddrescue` to extract the raw block file. |\n| 3.2 | Attempt to recover the **keystore** from the image. | The keystore holds the keys needed to decrypt user data. | \u2022\u202fElcomsoft Android Toolkit \u2013 \u201cAndroid Keystore\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic \u2013 \u201cKeystore Extraction\u201d. |\n| 3.3 | If the suspect\u2019s **passcode** or **Google credentials** are known (from other evidence or a warrant), use them to unlock the device. | Most forensic tools can decrypt ADB\u2011level backups with credentials. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite \u2013 \u201cAndroid Decryption\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen \u2013 \u201cPassword Recovery\u201d. |\n| 3.4 | If the device is in **Knox** mode, use **Knox forensics** (Samsung\u2019s own tool) to extract keys. | Knox stores keys in a protected \u201cKnox Vault\u201d that some tools can access. | Samsung Knox 4.0 Forensics Toolkit (if available). |\n| 3.5 | If all else fails, file a **motion to compel** the suspect\u2019s passcode or use **law\u2011enforced device\u2011unlock** procedures. | Only proceed if legal authority is secured. | Court order, DOJ/FSO guidance. |\n\n---\n\n### 4. \u2022\u202fOxygen \u2013 \u201cSamsung Location\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fFTK \u2013 \u201cSQLite DB\u201d parser. |\n| 4.4 | Pull **system logs** (`/data/system/` and `/data/system/users/0/`). | Contains Scene/Seizure Documentation\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 1.1 | Record seizure paperwork (warrant, date/time, location, officers, chain of custody log). | Creates legal pedigree and protects admissibility. | Standard forensic log template (Excel/Word). |\n| 1.2 | Photograph the device in its original state and the forensic bag. | Visual proof of condition at seizure. | Digital camera or forensic imaging kit. |\n| 1.3 | Note device condition (screen, battery, charging port, SIM tray). | Helps anticipate acquisition challenges. | Observation notes. |\n\n---\n\n### 2. Initial Forensic\u2011Safe Acquisition\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 2.1 | **Create a forensic image of the internal storage** (eMMC/SSD). | Raw, bit\u2011by\u2011bit copy preserves all artefacts, including deleted data. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer (Android 14 support)<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic Detective \u2013 \u201cPhysical Acquisition\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fMagnet AXIOM \u2013 \u201cPhysical Copy\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fIf device is unlockable, use `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f backup.ab` + `adb backup -n`. |\n| 2.2 | Compute and record SHA\u2011256 & MD5 of the image. | Enables later integrity verification. | `sha256sum img.dd` / `md5sum img.dd` (Linux) or FTK Imager. |\n| 2.3 | If the device is **locked** and you cannot unlock it, perform a **hardware\u2011level acquisition** (e.g., using a write\u2011blocker compatible with Samsung eMMC). | Some forensic tools can extract a full image even when the OS is locked. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer \u2013 \u201cHardware Acquisition\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic \u2013 \u201cDevice Acquisition\u201d (if supported). |\n| 2.4 | Verify image integrity with the original hash values. | Confirms that the image was not corrupted in transit. | Same tools as 2.2. |\n| 2.5 | Store the image in a write\u2011protected, access\u2011controlled storage (e.g., forensic server). | Prevents accidental tampering. | Encrypted NAS or dedicated forensic workstation. |\n\n---\n\n### 3. Device De\u2011Encryption (If Needed)\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 3.1 | Determine encryption status (Android 14 uses **File Based Encryption (FBE)** + **Device Owner** keys). | If the image is encrypted, you cannot read useful files. | `dd` + `ddrescue` to extract the raw block file. |\n| 3.2 | Attempt to recover the **keystore** from the image. | The keystore holds the keys needed to decrypt user data. | \u2022\u202fElcomsoft Android Toolkit \u2013 \u201cAndroid Keystore\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic \u2013 \u201cKeystore Extraction\u201d. |\n| 3.3 | If the suspect\u2019s **passcode** or **Google credentials** are known (from other evidence or a warrant), use them to unlock the device. | Most forensic tools can decrypt ADB\u2011level backups with credentials. | \u2022\u202fCellebrite \u2013 \u201cAndroid Decryption\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fOxygen \u2013 \u201cPassword Recovery\u201d. |\n| 3.4 | If the device is in **Knox** mode, use **Knox forensics** (Samsung\u2019s own tool) to extract keys. | Knox stores keys in a protected \u201cKnox Vault\u201d that some tools can access. | Samsung Knox 4.0 Forensics Toolkit (if available). |\n| 3.5 | If all else fails, file a **motion to compel** the suspect\u2019s passcode or use **law\u2011enforced device\u2011unlock** procedures. | Only proceed if legal authority is secured. | Court order, DOJ/FSO guidance. |\n\n---\n\n### 4. Logical Extraction of App & System Data\n\n| # | Step | Justification | Suggested Tool / Artefact |\n|---|------|---------------|---------------------------|\n| 4.1 | Run **logical extraction** (ADB pull of `/data/`, `/sdcard/`, `/system/`) on the decrypted image. | Provides high\u2011level view of installed apps, media, logs. | \u2022\u202fOxygen Forensic \u2013 \u201cLogical Extraction\u201d<br>\u2022\u202fCellebrite \u2013 \u201cLogical Extraction\u201d. |\n| 4.2 | Parse **Google Location History** (if enabled). | The most reliable source for GPS coordinates on A physical image is necessary to recover the FBE master key, which can later be used to decrypt the logical image.\n\n---\n\n## 3.\u202fValidation of the Image  \n| Step | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|------|---------------|----------------|\n| 3.1  | Verify that the image\u2019s checksums match the recorded values. | **HashCalc**, **md5sum**, or the hashing module inside the forensic tool. |\n| 3.2  | Create a **Forensic Work\u2011Space** (copy of the original image) and work on that to preserve the original. | Clone the image via **dd** or the tool\u2019s \u201cCreate Work Space\u201d feature. |\n\n---\n\n## 4.\u202fDevice Unlocking & Key Extraction  \n| Step | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|------|---------------|----------------|\n| 4.1  | A locked device cannot reveal user data. Store the checksums in the chain of custody file. | Tool\u2011provided hashing. |\n| 2.4  | **Logical acquisition** (pulling the \u201c/data\u201d partition) is useful for quick look\u2011ups of user data once the device is unlocked. | **Cellebrite UFOS**, **Oxygen**, **XRY**, or **ADB** (after unlocking). |\n\n> **Tip** \u2013 On a Samsung S23 the bootloader is typically *locked* and the device is *encrypted* with File\u2011Based Encryption (FBE). A physical image is necessary to recover the FBE master key, which can later be used to decrypt the logical image.\n\n---\n\n## 3.\u202fValidation of the Image  \n| Step | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|------|---------------|----------------|\n| 3.1  | Verify that the image\u2019s checksums match the recorded values. | **HashCalc**, **md5sum**, or the hashing module inside the forensic tool. |\n| 3.2  | Create a **Forensic Work\u2011Space** (copy of the original image) and work on that to preserve the original. | Clone the image via **dd** or the tool\u2019s \u201cCreate Work Space\u201d feature. |\n\n---\n\n## 4.\u202fDevice Unlocking & Key Extraction  \n| Step | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|------|---------------|----------------|\n| 4.1  | A locked device cannot reveal user data. The suspect\u2019s pass\u2011code/pattern/biometric must be legally authorized to be bypassed. | **Cellebrite Android Device Recovery** (brute\u2011force, dictionary, or passcode recovery). |\n| 4.2  | Extract the **File\u2011Based Encryption (FBE) master key** from the device\u2019s memory (if not already in the image). | **Oxygen Forensics** (Android Key Extraction module). |\n| 4.3  | Use the recovered master key to **decrypt the logical image**. | Same tool \u2013 the \u201cDecrypt\u201d function in UFOS, Oxygen, or XRY. |\n| 4.4  | Verify that the decrypted data is complete (file trees, timestamps). | Manual verification + tool audit. |\n\n> **Legal note** \u2013 Bypass of encryption must be performed under a court order or warrant. Document every step and keep a copy of the warrant.\n\n---\n\n## 5.\u202fAutomated Data Extraction (Logical Layer)  \n| Step | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|------|---------------|----------------|\n| 5.1  | Pull **system logs** (logcat, event logs). These contain timestamps for app launches, network events, and may reveal location services events. | **Cellebrite UFOS** (Logcat export), **Android Debug Bridge (adb)**. |\n| 5.2  | Pull **SMS/MMS** and **Call Log** databases. | **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet AXIOM**. |\n| 5.3  | Pull **Messaging apps** (WhatsApp, Telegram, Signal, Viber, Facebook Messenger). | **Oxygen**, **Cellebrite**, **ElcomSoft** (WhatsApp extraction). |\n| 5.4  | Pull **Calendar**, **Email**, **Browser History** (Chrome, Samsung Internet). | **Oxygen**, **Cellebrite**. |\n| 5.5  | Pull **App usage statistics** (if available). | **Android Usage Stats** table via **adb** or **Oxygen**. |\n| 5.6  | Pull **Battery & charging logs** \u2013 can indicate last usage before the device was turned off. | **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**. |\n| 5.7  | Pull **Wi\u2011Fi & Bluetooth scan logs** (saved in `wifi_lan`, `bluetooth_le_scan`). | **Oxygen**, **Cellebrite**. |\n| 5.8  | Pull **Photos & Video** with EXIF geotags (Samsung Gallery, Google Photos). | **Oxygen** (extract images + metadata). |\n| 5.9  | Pull **Google/ Samsung Cloud sync files** (if the device is synced). | **Google Takeout** (if you Quality\u2011Assurance Considerations\n\n1. **Chain of Custody** \u2013 Every transfer of the device or data must be logged with date, time, and sign\u2011off.  \n2. **Forensic Readiness** \u2013 Use tools that support **write\u2011blocker** and **hash\u2011generation** at acquisition.  \n3. **Data Integrity** \u2013 Store the original image in a write\u2011protected medium; all analysis must be performed on a copy.  \n4. **Authentication** \u2013 Use tool certificates and signed binaries to avoid tampering.  \n5. **Documentation** \u2013 Keep a detailed log of every tool version, command, and output.  \n6. **Legal Compliance** \u2013 Verify that the device was seized under a valid warrant and that all data extraction complies with local privacy laws (e.g., GDPR, CCPA).  \n\n---\n\n## 6.\u202fPotential Pitfalls & Mitigation\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| **Device encrypted with Knox** | Use **Cellebrite UFED** (supports Knox unlock) or request the encryption key from the manufacturer (if legally permissible). |\n| **Locked bootloader** | Physical extraction may still be possible; if not, rely on logical extraction and cloud data. |\n| **No Google/ Samsung account** | Focus on local logs (GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi) and third\u2011party data (telecom, Wi\u2011Fi hotspots). |\n| **Data deleted** | Physical extraction + undelete tools (e.g., **Recuva**, **PhotoRec**) to recover deleted files. |\n| **App encryption** | Use **Elcomsoft Phone Breaker** or **Oxygen Forensics** to decrypt common messaging apps. |\n| **Time\u2011zone discrepancies** | Convert all timestamps to UTC and cross\u2011check with device clock. |\n\n---\n\n## 7.\u202fSample Workflow (Illustrative)\n\n1. **Scene** \u2013 Photograph the device, seal it in a Faraday bag, sign CoC.  \n2. **Acquisition** \u2013 Connect to UFED, perform a **physical image** (if possible).  \n3. **Hash** \u2013 Compute SHA\u2011256, store in evidence log.  \n4. **Unlock** \u2013 Use UFED\u2019s pass\u2011code bypass; if fails, try Elcomsoft.  \n5. **Logical extraction** \u2013 Pull all user data, system logs, and app artefacts.  \n6. **Parse** \u2013 Run the **Location** module in UFED/AXIOM; export GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi logs.  \n7. **Cross\u2011check** \u2013 Map cell IDs to coordinates using CellMapper; compare with Wi\u2011Fi BSSIDs.  \n8. **Timeline** \u2013 Import all timestamps into **Chronology**; filter for 15\u202fJan\u202f2024.  \n9. **Validate** \u2013 Verify that the GPS timestamps match the device clock and that no gaps exist.  \n10. **Report** \u2013 Compile findings, attach screenshots, hash values, and a narrative explaining the suspect\u2019s movements.  \n\n---\n\n## 8.\u202fConclusion\n\nBy following the above methodology, investigators can:\n\n1. **Reconstruct** the suspect\u2019s location on the day of the murder with high confidence.  \n2. **Uncover** additional evidence (communications, financial activity, media) that may support motive, alibi, or co\u2011conspirators.  \n3. **Maintain** the evidentiary chain and comply with legal standards, ensuring the findings are admissible in court.\n\nThe key is to **preserve the device\u2019s integrity**, **extract all recoverable data**, and **correlate device artefacts with external logs**. tools that support **write\u2011blocker** and **hash\u2011generation** at acquisition.  \n3. **Data Integrity** \u2013 Store the original image in a write\u2011protected medium; all analysis must be 6.\u202fPotential Pitfalls & Mitigation\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| **Device encrypted with Knox** | Use **Cellebrite UFED** (supports Knox unlock) or request the encryption key from the manufacturer (if legally permissible). |\n| **Locked bootloader** | Physical extraction may still be possible; if not, rely on logical extraction and cloud data. |\n| **No Google/ Samsung account** | Focus on local logs (GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi) and third\u2011party data (telecom, Wi\u2011Fi hotspots). |\n| **Data deleted** | Physical extraction + undelete tools (e.g., **Recuva**, **PhotoRec**) to recover deleted files. |\n| **App encryption** | Use **Elcomsoft Phone Breaker** or **Oxygen Forensics** to decrypt common messaging apps. |\n| **Time\u2011zone discrepancies** | Convert all timestamps to UTC and cross\u2011check with device clock. |\n\n---\n\n## 7.\u202fSample Workflow (Illustrative)\n\n1. **Scene** \u2013 Photograph the device, seal it in a Faraday bag, sign UFED\u2019s pass\u2011code bypass; if fails, try Elcomsoft.  \n5. **Logical extraction** \u2013 Pull all user data, system logs, and app artefacts.  \n6. **Parse** \u2013 Run the **Location** module in UFED/AXIOM; export GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi logs.  \n7. **Cross\u2011check** \u2013 Map cell IDs to coordinates using CellMapper; compare with Wi\u2011Fi BSSIDs.  \n8. **Timeline** \u2013 Import all timestamps into **Chronology**; filter for 15\u202fJan\u202f2024.  \n9. **Validate** \u2013 Verify that the GPS timestamps match the device clock and that no gaps exist.  \n10. **Report** \u2013 Compile findings, attach screenshots, hash values, and a narrative explaining the suspect\u2019s movements.  \n\n---\n\n## 8.\u202fConclusion\n\nBy following the above methodology, investigators |\n|----------|--------------|---------------------------|\n| **GPS coordinates** (timestamped) | Direct proof of location. | Android `location` database, Google Location History, Samsung Cloud |\n| **Cell\u2011Tower ID** (MCC/MNC/LAC/CellID) | Approximate location when GPS off. | `telephony` logs, `cell_towers` database, `logcat` |\n| **Wi\u2011Fi SSID/BSSID** | Pinpointing proximity to known hotspots. | `wifi` logs, `network` database |\n| **Bluetooth LE** | Nearby devices (e.g., a car, a friend\u2019s phone). | `bluetooth_le` database |\n| **Find My Mobile** | Last known location, device Short\u2011term location snapshots. | WhatsApp, Telegram, Signal, Instagram, Snapchat, TikTok, etc. |\n\nBy correlating these artefacts, you can build a **high\u2011confidence timeline** of the suspect\u2019s whereabouts on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024.\n\n---\n\n## 4.\u202fSecondary Evidence That May Be Relevant\n\n| Category | Potential Insight | Extraction Tool **Financial** | Money flow, possible motive. | Cellebrite/AXIOM (PayPal, Venmo, Google Pay, Samsung Pay) |\n| **Browser History** | Search terms, visited sites. | Cellebrite/AXIOM (Chrome, Samsung app). | Cellebrite/AXIOM (App usage logs) |\n| **System Logs** | Device state, battery, crashes. | Logcat, `system` logs, `dmesg` |\n| **Cloud Backups** | Data not present on the device. | Samsung Cloud, Google Drive, Dropbox, OneDrive |\n| **Metadata** | Device model, IMEI, serial number, Android version. | Device info extraction (Cellebrite/AXIOM) |\n\n---\n\n## 5.\u202fLegal & Quality\u2011Assurance Considerations\n\n1. **Chain of Custody** \u2013 Every transfer of the device or data must be logged with date, time, and sign\u2011off.  \n2. **Forensic Readiness** \u2013 Use tools that support **write\u2011blocker** and **hash\u2011generation** at acquisition.  \n3. **Data Integrity** \u2013 Store the original image in a write\u2011protected medium; all analysis must be performed on a copy.  \n4. **Authentication** \u2013 Use tool certificates and signed binaries to avoid tampering.  \n5. **Documentation** \u2013 Keep a detailed log of every tool version, command, and output.  \n6. **Legal Compliance** \u2013 Verify that the device was seized under a valid warrant and that all data extraction complies with local privacy laws (e.g., GDPR, CCPA).  \n\n---\n\n## 6.\u202fPotential Pitfalls & Mitigation\n\n| Issue | Mitigation |\n|-------|------------|\n| **Device encrypted with Knox** | Use **Cellebrite UFED** (supports Knox unlock) or request the encryption key from the manufacturer (if legally permissible). |\n| **Locked bootloader** | Physical extraction may still be possible; if not, rely on logical extraction and cloud data. |\n| **No Google/ Samsung account** | Focus on local logs (GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi) and third\u2011party data (telecom, Wi\u2011Fi hotspots). |\n| **Data deleted** | Physical extraction + undelete tools (e.g., **Recuva**, **PhotoRec**) to recover deleted files. |\n| **App encryption** | Use **Elcomsoft Phone Breaker** or **Oxygen Forensics** to decrypt common messaging apps. |\n| **Time\u2011zone discrepancies** | Convert all timestamps to UTC and cross\u2011check with device clock. |\n\n---\n\n## 7.\u202fSample Workflow (Illustrative)\n\n1. **Scene** \u2013 Photograph the device, seal it in a Faraday bag, sign CoC.  \n2. **Acquisition** \u2013 Connect to UFED, perform a **physical image** (if possible).  \n3. **Hash** \u2013 Compute SHA\u2011256, store in evidence log.  \n4. **Unlock** \u2013 Use UFED\u2019s pass\u2011code bypass; if fails, try Elcomsoft.  \n5. **Logical extraction** \u2013 Pull all user data, system logs, and app artefacts.  \n6. **Parse** \u2013 Run the **Location** module in UFED/AXIOM; export GPS, cell, Wi\u2011Fi logs.  \n7. **Cross\u2011check** \u2013 Map cell IDs to coordinates using CellMapper; compare with Wi\u2011Fi BSSIDs.  \n8. **Timeline** \u2013 Import all timestamps into **Chronology**; filter for 15\u202fJan\u202f2024.  \n9. **Validate** \u2013 Verify that the GPS timestamps match the device clock and that no gaps exist.  \n10. **Report** \u2013 Compile findings, attach screenshots, hash values, and a narrative explaining the suspect\u2019s movements.  \n\n---\n\n## 8.\u202fConclusion\n\nBy following the above methodology, investigators can:\n\n1. **Reconstruct** the suspect\u2019s location on the day of the murder with high confidence.  \n2. **Uncover** additional evidence (communications, financial activity, media) that may support motive, alibi, or co\u2011conspirators.  \n3. **Maintain** the evidentiary chain and comply with legal standards, ensuring the findings are admissible in court.\n\nThe key is to **preserve the device\u2019s integrity**, **extract all recoverable data**, and **correlate device artefacts with external logs**. The tools listed above are industry\u2011standard, well\u2011documented, and provide the necessary forensic rigor for a case of this magnitude.<|return|>",

Evidence acquisition & chain of custody\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 1.1 | **Log the seizure** \u2013 Document device serial, IMEI, state of charge, any visible accessories, and the environment. | Provides context and baseline for later comparisons. | Standard seizure sheet, camera (for photos), a forensic notebook. |\n| 1.2 | **Create a write\u2011protected forensic image** \u2013 Use a hardware\u2011based \u201cwrite\u2011blocker\u201d (e.g., Cellebrite UFED\u2011Hardware, Oxygen Forensic Physical Acquisition). | Prevents accidental modification and preserves the original. | Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer, Oxygen Forensic Physical Analyzer, Magnet AXIOM (hardware mode). |\n| 1.3 | **Generate hash values** (SHA\u2011256, MD5) of the raw image and store them in a tamper\u2011evident log. | Verifies integrity during later stages. | HashCalc, FTK Imager, WinHash. |\n| 1.4 | **Maintain a detailed chain of custody** \u2013 Record every person who handled the device and the image, date/time, and purpose. | Required for admissibility. | Chain of custody form (digital or paper), timestamped logs. |\n\n---\n\n### 2. Preliminary device assessment\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 2.1 | **Determine encryption status & root level** \u2013 Inspect bootloader state, verify \u201cOEM unlocking\u201d flag, check for Knox. | Determines whether a *physical* extraction can read the file system or if a *logical* extraction is required. | UFED, Oxygen, `adb shell` (if device can boot to recovery). |\n| 2.2 | **Capture device metadata** \u2013 IMEI, MEID, Android ID, OS version, firmware build, installed security patches. | Useful for context and cross\u2011checking with other evidence (e.g., SIM logs). | UFED, Oxygen, EnCase, `adb shell getprop`. |\n| 2.3 | **Verify secure element / Knox status** \u2013 Check if the device uses Samsung Knox or an external secure element. | Determines whether additional forensic kits (e.g., Samsung Knox SDK) are needed to decrypt the device. | Samsung Knox SDK, UFED. |\n\n---\n\n### 3. Full logical/physical data extraction\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 3.1 | **Physical extraction** \u2013 Pull the raw NV\u2011flash image or a full file system image. | Captures everything, including deleted files and hidden partitions. | UFED Physical Analyzer, Oxygen Forensic Physical Analyzer, Magnet AXIOM (physical mode). |\n| 3.2 | **Logical extraction** \u2013 Pull app data, contacts, SMS, call logs, etc. | Provides a human\u2011readable view of structured data that may not be fully recoverable from the raw image. | UFED Logical Analyzer, Oxygen Forensic Logical Analyzer, Magnet AXIOM (logical mode). |\n| 3.3 | **Extract encrypted containers** \u2013 If the device is encrypted, use the device's de\u2011cryption key (provided by the suspect\u2019s Samsung account or via a *device\u2011side* extraction supported by the tool). | Allows access to all protected data. | UFED with Knox/Android decryption, Oxygen (Android 10+ decryption). |\n| 3.4 | **Pull cloud\u2011synchronised data** \u2013 Access Google Drive, Samsung Cloud, OneDrive, etc. (with proper authorisation). | Cloud copies may contain data not present locally (e.g., older photos, older location history). | UFED Cloud Access, Oxygen Cloud Access, Elcomsoft Cloud Explorer. |\n\n---\n\n### 4. Extraction of **location information**\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 4.1 | **Raw GPS logs** \u2013 Pull `/data/misc/location/` and `/data/system/location/` (Android\u202f10+) and `/data/system/gps/` (older). | Contains timestamped latitude/longitude pairs produced by the Android Location Provider. | UFED, Oxygen (file extraction), custom Python script to parse `*.log` or `*.json`. |\n| 4.2 | **Google Location History** \u2013 Pull `/data/data/com.google.android.gms/databases/lh.db` or the JSON export from the Google account. | Gives a high\u2011resolution GPS log (if the user had \u201cLocation History\u201d enabled). | UFED, Oxygen, `adb pull`, ExifTool on the exported JSON. |\n| 4.3 | **Samsung Find\u2011My\u2011Mobile data** \u2013 Pull `/data/knox/` or the `findmydevice` database. | Samsung\u2019s own service records the device\u2019s last known location. | UFED, Oxygen, Samsung Knox SDK. |\n| 4.4 | **Wi\u2011Fi SSID logs** \u2013 Pull `WifiConfigStore.xml`, `last_scanned.xml`. | Each SSID includes a timestamp and signal strength, useful for triangulating position when GPS is unavailable. | UFED, Oxygen, ExifTool, custom XML parser. |\n| 4.5 | **Cell\u2011tower logs** \u2013 Pull `/data/misc/telephony/` or use the Telephony Manager logs (if available). | Triangulation using serving cell and neighbouring cells. | UFED, Oxygen, custom scripts. |\n| 4.6 | **Bluetooth logs** \u2013 Pull `bluetooth_le` logs (`/data/misc/bluetooth/`). | Nearby devices can corroborate a location. | UFED, Oxygen, custom parser. |\n| 4.7 | **App\u2011specific location data** \u2013 Extract from apps that store location (Google Maps, Waze, Uber, Grab, Instagram, Snapchat, WhatsApp, Discord). | Many apps keep a \u201ctimeline\u201d or \u201clocation history\u201d that may be more granular than the system logs. | UFED, Oxygen, Belkasoft, custom app parsers (`.db` files). |\n\n---\n\n### 5. Evidence acquisition & chain of custody\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 1.1 | **Log the seizure** \u2013 Document device serial, IMEI, state of charge, any visible accessories, and the environment. | Provides context and baseline for later comparisons. | Standard seizure sheet, camera (for photos), a forensic notebook. |\n| 1.2 | **Create a write\u2011protected forensic image** \u2013 Use a hardware\u2011based \u201cwrite\u2011blocker\u201d (e.g., Cellebrite UFED\u2011Hardware, Oxygen Forensic Physical Acquisition). | Prevents accidental modification and preserves the original. | Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer, Oxygen Forensic Physical Analyzer, Magnet AXIOM (hardware mode). |\n| 1.3 | **Generate hash values** (SHA\u2011256, MD5) of the raw image and store them in a tamper\u2011evident log. | Verifies integrity during later stages. | HashCalc, FTK Imager, WinHash. |\n| 1.4 | **Maintain a detailed chain of custody** \u2013 Record every person who handled the device and the image, date/time, and purpose. | Required for admissibility. | Chain of custody form (digital or paper), timestamped logs. |\n\n---\n\n### 2. Preliminary device assessment\n\n| Step | Action | Justification | Tool(s) |\n|------|--------|--------------|---------|\n| 2.1 | **Determine encryption status & root level** \u2013 Inspect bootloader state, verify \u201cOEM unlocking\u201d flag, check for Knox. | Determines whether a *physical* extraction can read the file system or if a *logical* extraction is required. | UFED, Oxygen, `adb shell` (if device can boot to recovery). |\n| 2.2 | **Capture device metadata** \u2013 IMEI, MEID, Android ID, OS version, firmware build, installed security patches. | Useful for context and cross\u2011checking with other evidence (e.g., SIM logs). | UFED, Oxygen, EnCase, `adb shell getprop`. |\n| 2.3 | **Verify secure element / Knox status** \u2013 Check if the device uses Samsung Knox or an external secure element. | Determines whether additional forensic kits (e.g., Samsung Knox SDK) are needed to decrypt the device. | Samsung Knox SDK, UFED. |\n\n---\n\n### 3. Document every step with timestamps and signed logs.  \n2. **Device Encryption** \u2013 Samsung S23 uses full\u2011device encryption and Knox. If the suspect\u2019s pass\u2011code is unavailable, use a Knox\u2011aware tool that can recover the decryption key from the device\u2019s secure element.  \n3. **Data Volatility** \u2013 If the phone is still powered on, capture a volatile memory snapshot (`adb pull /proc`) before powering down.  \n4. **Multiple Acquisition Methods** \u2013 When in doubt, perform both a logical and a physical acquisition; any data that appears in one but not the other warrants further investigation.  \n5. **Third\u2011Party Forensic Modules** \u2013 Many commercial tools now include modules for popular messaging apps and cloud services. Seizure & Documentation  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool / Record |\n|---|--------|---------------|--------------------------|\n| 1.1 | **Photograph the device and its surroundings** (case, charger, OS\u2011level lock screen, any visible stickers). | Creates a visual record that can be referred to if the phone is damaged or the chain of custody is questioned. | Digital camera / phone, sealed evidence bag. |\n| 1.2 | **Write a detailed seizure log** (time, location, officers, condition, battery level, display status, presence of a SIM, whether the device was powered on). | Provides the first point of integrity; required for admissibility. | Standard evidence log template. |\n| 1.3 | **Seal the phone in a tamper\u2011evident bag** and apply a unique identifier (e.g., \u201cEVID\u2011S23\u2011001\u201d). | Prevents post\u2011seizure tampering. | Evidence bag with tamper seal. |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Chain of Custody & Evidence Integrity  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|---|--------|---------------|----------------|\n| 2.1 | **Create a chain\u2011of\u2011custody sheet** and have every person who handles the device sign it. | Establishes a legally admissible record of who owned the evidence. | Paper sheet or digital COC system. |\n| 2.2 | **Calculate a cryptographic hash (SHA\u2011256)** of the original device state (e.g., the screen display, battery level, or a small \u201cseed\u201d file). | Provides a baseline fingerprint that can be checked after acquisition. | `shannon` or `md5sum \u2013s` on a PC. |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Initial Device Assessment  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|---|--------|---------------|----------------|\n| 3.1 | **Determine if the device is powered on and if the screen is unlocked.** | Knowing the lock state decides whether we can get a *physical* or only a *logical* image. | Observation, remote\u2011access if possible. |\n| 3.2 | **Check for \u201cFind My Mobile\u201d or \u201cFind My Device\u201d status** via the web or a test device. | If the account is active, we can pull the last known location from the cloud. | Web browser, Samsung/Google account portals. |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Acquire a **Physical Image** (if device is unlocked)\\,  \n\n> *If the device is locked, skip to Section\u202f5 (logical acquisition).*  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|---|--------|---------------|----------------|\n| 4.1 | **Connect the phone to a forensic workstation via a write\u2011blocker** (e.g., \u201cCellebrite Write\u2011Blocker\u201d or a custom USB\u2011OTG blocker). | Prevents inadvertent modification of the device. | Physical write\u2011blocker. |\n| 4.2 | **Run a full physical acquisition** with a commercial tool that supports Android 14 and Samsung Knox. | Physical acquisition reads the raw flash memory, giving us decrypted partitions when Knox is active. | **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer**, **Oxygen Forensics Detective** (Android 14 support), or **Magnet AXIOM**. |\n| 4.3 | **Verify the integrity of the image** by comparing the computed SHA\u2011256 against the pre\u2011acquisition hash. | Confirms that the image is identical to the seized device. | `sha256sum` on the forensic workstation. |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Acquire a **Logical Image** (if the device is locked)\\,  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|---|--------|---------------|----------------|\n| 5.1 | **Use a logical acquisition** that can read the Android filesystem even when locked, leveraging the \u201cAndroid Device Manager\u201d / \u201cKnox\u201d fallback. | Provides most user\u2011level data (apps, contacts, SMS, etc.) without needing the PIN. | **Cellebrite UFED Logical**, **Oxygen Forensics Detective** (Android 14), **Magnet AXIOM**. |\n| 5.2 | **Attempt an ADB backup** (if \u201cUSB debugging\u201d is enabled). | Gives a filesystem snapshot that may contain more logs than the logical acquisition. | `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f backup.ab` |\n\n\n> **Tip:**  \n> If the phone is completely locked and no backup exists, you may need to resort to **Knox decryption** or **chip\u2011off**. For the S23, Cellebrite\u2019s *Knox* module can sometimes recover the \u201cKnox Key\u201d if the device is still on and the user has not performed a wipe. If that fails, bring in a mobile\u2011device\u2011forensic (MDF) lab for JTAG / chip\u2011off.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Unlock / Decrypt the Phone (if necessary)\\,  \n\n| # | Action | Justification | Suggested Tool |\n|---|--------|---------------|----------------|\n| 6.1 | **Try to unlock with the suspect\u2019s credentials** (PIN, pattern, password, biometric). | The cleanest path to a full forensic image. | Standard unlock process. |\n| 6.2 | **Use Samsung Smart Switch or \u201cFind My Mobile\u201d** to reset the lock screen if the user has a backup. | Bypass the lock screen while preserving data. | Samsung Smart Switch (Windows). |\n| 6.3 | **Invoke the device\u2019s Knox \u201cDevice Owner\u201d unlock** if the phone is enrolled in a corporate MDM. | Knox provides a decryption key that can be used by Cellebrite. | Cellebrite UFED Physical + Knox module. |\n| 6.4 | **If all else fails, perform a forensic chip\u2011off** (JTAG / chip\u2011off) to read the NAND flash directly. | Last\u2011resort method for fully encrypted, locked phones. | JTAG hardware, proprietary firmware extraction tools. |\n\n> **Legal note:**  \n> Any attempt to bypass the lock screen must be documented and justified; otherwise, it may be challenged in court.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extract **Location Data** from the Phone  \n\n| # | Source | What to Look For | Why It Helps | Suggested Tool |\n|---|---------|------------------|--------------|----------------|\n| 7.1 | **/data/system/location/location_history.db** (Android) | `lat`, `lon`, `timestamp`, `accuracy` | Official Android location history (if the user enabled \u201cLocation History\u201d). | **SQLite3**, **Oxygen Forensics**, **Magnet** |\n| 7.2 | **/data/adb/knox/knox.db** (Knox) | `knox_location`, `knox_timestamp` | Knox stores its own location logs; often more frequent and covers the lock screen. | **SQLite3**, **Oxygen** |\n| 7.3 | **Google Play Services \u201cFusedLocationProvider\u201d logs** | `com.google.android.gms.location` content provider | Gives accurate, high\u2011frequency updates. | **Cellebrite Logical** (if provider data is exported) |\n| 7.4 | **Google Maps Timeline** (cloud) | `lat`, `lon`, `timestamp`, `deviceID` | Cloud backup of location history; check** \u2013 Power on, note battery level, check for a screen lock.  \n3. **Image acquisition** \u2013  \n   * If the device is unlocked: `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f device.ab` (creates an Android backup).  \n   * If locked: use **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** to pull a full image (Android 14).  \n4. **SIM extraction** \u2013 Insert SIM into a reader, run **Cellebrite** SIM module.  \n5. **Backup extraction** \u2013  \n   * Google: request a **Takeout** of Location History.  \n   * Samsung: run **Smart Switch** to pull a local backup if available.  \n6. **RAM dump** \u2013 If the device is rooted or the forensic tool supports it, run `adb shell su -c \"cat /dev/mem > /sdcard/ramdump.bin\"`.  \n7. **Log extraction** \u2013 `adb logcat -d > logcat.txt`.  \n8. /system/build.prop`.  \n12. **Network logs** \u2013 Pull Wi\u2011Fi config and BSSID logs.  \n13. **Sensor logs** \u2013 If present, pull `/data/system/sensor/`.  \n14. **Timeline creation** \u2013 Import all timestamps into **Magnet AXIOM** or **Oxygen** and generate a timeline.  \n15. **Integrity check** \u2013 Compute SHA\u2011256 of every file and record in the chain of custody.  \n16. **Reporting** \u2013 Export a PDF report that includes:  \n    * Device metadata.  \n    * Location timeline for 15\u202fJan\u202f2024 (map overlay).  \n    * Relevant communications (redacted).  \n    * Any evidence of travel or contact with the victim.  \n17. **Legal review** \u2013 Verify that all steps meet local forensic standards and that the chain of custody is complete.  \n\n---\n\n### Key check** \u2013 Power on, note battery level, check for a screen lock.  \n3. **Image acquisition** \u2013  \n   * If the device is unlocked: `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f device.ab` (creates an check** \u2013 Power on, note battery level, check for a screen lock.  \n3. **Image acquisition** \u2013  \n   * If the device is unlocked: `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f device.ab` (creates an  * Any evidence of travel or contact with the victim.  \n17. **Legal review** \u2013 Verify that all steps meet local forensic standards and that the chain of custody is complete.  \n\n---\n\n### Key methodology that will let you (1) pinpoint the suspect's location on\u202f15\u202fJan\u202f2024 and (2) surface any other data that may be useful to the homicide investigation.  \nEach step contains:\n\n| # | Step | Why it matters | Primary tools / commands |\n|---|------|----------------|--------------------------|\n| 1 | **Secure the scene & create a chain of custody** | Prevents contamination, establishes admissibility. | Evidence bag, sealed evidence label, chain of custody form, forensic evidence\u2011management system (e.g., FTK, EnCase). |\n| 2 | **Initial device assessment** | Determines battery state, connectivity, encryption status, and whether the device is in a \u201clocked\u201d or \u201cunlocked\u201d state. | Physical inspection, quick\u2011look with a forensic reader (e.g., Cellebrite UFED), `adb` (if unlocked). |\n| 3 | **Acquire a forensic image of internal storage** | Preserves the exact byte stream for all subsequent analysis. | **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** (Android 14 support), **Oxygen Forensics Detective**, **Magnet AXIOM**, **Elcomsoft Phone Viewer**. |\n| 4 | **Acquire a forensic image of external storage (microSD)** | Some apps store media or logs on the SD card. | Same tools as step\u202f3, or a dedicated SD\u2011card reader. |\n| 5 | **Extract the SIM card** | Call/SMS logs, contacts, and sometimes location data are stored on the SIM. | **Cellebrite UFED**, **Oxygen**, **Elcomsoft**, or a dedicated **SIM\u2011card reader**. |\n| 6 | **Pull a full device backup (Google Drive / Samsung Cloud)** | Backups often contain data that is not present on the device (e.g., deleted photos, older location history). | **Google Takeout** (via the suspect\u2019s Google account, if available), **Samsung Smart Switch** (if a local backup exists). |\n| 7 | **Acquire a RAM dump** | Volatile data (open apps, recent GPS fixes, active network connections) is only in memory. | **Cellebrite UFED**, **Magnet AXIOM**, **Volatility** (if you can dump `/dev/mem`). |\n| 8 | **Collect system logs** | `logcat`, `dmesg`, and Android event logs can reveal app crashes, location requests, and network activity. | `adb logcat -d > logcat.txt`, `adb shell dumpsys`, **Cellebrite** or **Oxygen** log extraction modules. |\n| 9 | **Recover location data** | The core of the first question. | \u2022 **Google Location History** (`/data/system/location/` or via Google Takeout). <br>\u2022 **Samsung Location Service** (`/data/system/location/` or `/data/system/knox/`). <br>\u2022 **Knox logs** (`/data/knox/`). <br>\u2022 **GPS raw logs** (`/data/system/gps/`). <br>\u2022 **Wi\u2011Fi/BLE proximity logs** (`/data/system/wifi/`). <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**, **Elcomsoft**, **ADB** (`adb pull`). |\n| 10 | **Recover communications** | Call/SMS/MMS, WhatsApp, Telegram, Signal, etc. can provide motive, alibi, or evidence of travel. | `adb pull /data/data/com.android.providers.telephony/databases/mmssms.db` <br>WhatsApp: `adb pull /data/data/com.whatsapp/databases/wa.db` <br>Telegram: `adb pull /data/data/org.telegram.messenger/databases/` <br>Signal: `adb pull /data/data/org.thoughtcrime.securesms/databases/` <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**, **Elcomsoft**. |\n| 11 | **Recover app data & logs** | Many apps (e.g., Instagram, Snapchat, Uber) store timestamps, geotags, and chat logs. | `adb pull /data/data/<package>/` <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**, **Elcomsoft**. |\n| 12 | **Extract device metadata** | IMEI, serial, OS version, firmware, and Knox status help verify the device and may link it to other evidence. | `adb shell getprop` <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**. |\n| 13 | **Collect network\u2011related data** | Wi\u2011Fi SSIDs, BSSIDs, IP addresses, and captive\u2011portal logs can place the device at a specific venue. | `adb pull /data/system/wifi/WifiConfigStore.xml` <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**. |\n| 14 | **Recover sensor logs** | Accelerometer/gyroscope data can confirm movement patterns or a \u201cwalk\u2011through\u201d of a location. | `adb pull /data/system/sensor/` <br>Tools: **Cellebrite**, **Oxygen**, **Magnet**. |\n| 15 | **Create a forensic timeline** | Correlating timestamps from all sources (GPS, logs, app data) gives a coherent picture of the suspect\u2019s movements. | **Magnet AXIOM**, **Oxygen Forensics**, **Cellebrite UFED**, **FTK**, **Autopsy**. |\n| 16 | **Validate evidence integrity** | Hashes prove that the data has not been altered. | SHA\u2011256/MD5 calculation in the forensic tool, or external `sha256sum`. |\n| 17 | **Document findings & produce a report** | A clear, court\u2011ready narrative is required. | Built\u2011in reporting modules of the forensic tools, or a custom report template. |\n| 18 | **Answer the investigative questions** | 1) **Location on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024** \u2013 GPS coordinates, Wi\u2011Fi/BLE proximity, and any location history entries that fall on that date. 2) **Other relevant elements** \u2013 e.g., deleted messages, app usage that indicates travel, financial transactions, or evidence of a \u201csecure folder\u201d that may contain hidden data. | Use the timeline and cross\u2011reference all data sources. |\n| 19 | **Recommend further actions** | If encryption or a secure folder blocks access, consider a **Knox\u2011aware extraction** or a **Samsung Smart Switch** backup. | **Cellebrite UFED**, **Oxygen**, **Elcomsoft**, **Samsung Smart Switch**. |\n| 20 | **Legal compliance** | Ensure all steps meet local forensic standards (e.g., ISO/IEC\u202f27037, NIST SP\u202f800\u2011101). | Maintain chain of custody, use validated tools, document every action. |\n\n---\n\n### Detailed justification & tool rationale\n\n| Step | Why it is essential | Tool justification |\n|------|---------------------|---------------------|\n| 1 | **Chain of custody** is the legal backbone of any digital evidence. | Evidence bags, sealed labels, and a digital evidence\u2011management system prevent tampering and provide a verifiable audit trail. |\n| 2 | Knowing whether the device is locked or encrypted determines the extraction strategy. | A quick `adb` test (`adb devices`) tells you if the device is unlocked; a physical reader (Cellebrite) can still pull a full image even if locked. |\n| 3 | A **bit\u2011exact image** is the only defensible source for all subsequent analysis. | UFED, Oxygen, Magnet, and Elcomsoft all support Android 14 and can pull the entire `/data` partition, preserving timestamps and file attributes. |\n| 4 | External media may hold deleted or older data. | The same tools can image an SD card; a dedicated reader is often faster and less intrusive. |\n| 5 | SIM cards store call/SMS logs and sometimes contacts. | Dedicated SIM readers can pull the `SIM` database; many forensic suites have a SIM extraction module. |\n| 6 | Backups may contain data that was deleted from the device. | Google Takeout can export Location History, Drive files, and more; Samsung Smart Switch can pull a local backup if the suspect used it. |\n| 7 | **RAM** contains transient data that is not written to disk. | A RAM dump can reveal the last GPS fix, open apps, or a cached location that is no longer on disk. |\n| 8 | System logs can show when the device requested location, when apps crashed, or when network connections were made. | `logcat` and `dumpsys` provide a rich source of timestamps that can be cross\u2011checked against GPS logs. |\n| 9 | **Location data** is the core of the first question. | Google Location History is the most reliable source; Samsung\u2019s own location service and Knox logs can fill gaps if the user disabled Google services. |\n| 10 | Communications can confirm the suspect\u2019s alibi or reveal a link to the victim. | Pulling the raw SQLite databases preserves all metadata (timestamps, thread IDs). |\n| 11 | App data may contain geotagged photos, chat logs, or ride\u2011share receipts. | Many apps store data in `/data/data/<package>/` \u2013 pulling the entire directory preserves all files. |\n| 12 | Device identifiers can be matched to other evidence (e.g., CCTV, other phones). | `getprop` returns IMEI, serial, and OS version; these are often used in cross\u2011device correlation. |\n| 13 | Wi\u2011Fi/BLE logs can place the phone at a specific venue even if GPS was off. | The `WifiConfigStore.xml` file lists all SSIDs the phone has connected to, with timestamps. |\n| 14 | Sensor logs can confirm movement patterns (e.g., walking vs. driving). | Some manufacturers log raw sensor data; if present, it can be parsed with custom scripts or forensic tools. |\n| 15 | A **timeline** is the narrative that ties all data together. | Most forensic suites can merge timestamps from multiple sources into a single, sortable view. |\n| 16 | Hashes prove that the evidence has not been altered during analysis. | Every tool can compute SHA\u2011256; store the hash in the chain of custody record. |\n| 17 | A clear report is required for the court. | Built\u2011in reporting modules produce PDF/HTML reports that include evidence images, hash values, and analysis notes. |\n| 18 | The investigative questions are answered by correlating the timeline with GPS coordinates and other logs. | The report should include a map overlay of the suspect\u2019s movements on 15\u202fJan\u202f2024. |\n| 19 | If encryption or a secure folder blocks access, specialized extraction methods are needed. | Samsung\u2019s **Knox** framework can be leveraged by tools that support Knox extraction; otherwise, a **Smart Switch** backup may be the only way to recover the data. |\n| 20 | Adhering to forensic standards ensures the evidence will be admissible. | Document every step, use validated tools, and keep the chain of custody intact. |\n\n---\n\n### Practical workflow example\n\n1. **Scene control** \u2013 Photograph the device, seal it, and log the seizure.  \n2. **Device check** \u2013 Power on, note battery level, check for a screen lock.  \n3. **Image acquisition** \u2013  \n   * If the device is unlocked: `adb backup -apk -shared -all -f device.ab` (creates an Android backup).  \n   * If locked: use **Cellebrite UFED Physical Analyzer** to pull a full image (Android 14).  \n4. **SIM extraction** \u2013 Insert SIM into a reader, run **Cellebrite** SIM module.  \n5. **Backup extraction** \u2013  \n   * Google: request a **Takeout** of Location History.  \n   * Samsung: run **Smart Switch** to pull a local backup if available.  \n6. **RAM dump** \u2013 If the device is rooted or the forensic tool supports it, run `adb shell su -c \"cat /dev/mem > /sdcard/ramdump.bin\"`.  \n7. **Log extraction** \u2013 `adb logcat -d > logcat.txt`.  \n8. **Location data** \u2013  \n   * Pull `/data/system/location/` and `/data/system/knox/`.  \n   * Parse with **Cellebrite** or custom Python scripts (`pylocation`).  \n9. **Communications** \u2013 Pull the SQLite databases for SMS, WhatsApp, Telegram, Signal.  \n10. **App data** \u2013 Pull `/data/data/` directories for key apps.  \n11. **Metadata** \u2013 Run `adb shell getprop` and `adb shell cat /system/build.prop`.  \n12. **Network logs** \u2013 Pull Wi\u2011Fi config and BSSID logs.  \n13. **Sensor logs** \u2013 If present, pull `/data/system/sensor/`.  \n14. **Timeline creation** \u2013 Import all timestamps into **Magnet AXIOM** or **Oxygen** and generate a timeline.  \n15. **Integrity check** \u2013 Compute SHA\u2011256 of every file and record in the chain of custody.  \n16. **Reporting** \u2013 Export a PDF report that includes:  \n    * Device metadata.  \n    * Location timeline for 15\u202fJan\u202f2024 (map overlay).  \n    * Relevant communications (redacted).  \n    * Any evidence of travel or contact with the victim.  \n17. **Legal review** \u2013 Verify that all steps meet local forensic standards and that the chain of custody is complete.  \n\n---\n\n### Key
